## User

How to make Liquid Glass menu bar in iOS app

---

## Assistant

You do it by layering **blur + tint + rounded shape** behind your buttons, then letting content scroll underneath it.

Below is how to build a ŌĆ£liquid glassŌĆØ style menu bar in **SwiftUI** (iOS 15+), and then a **UIKit** version.

---

## SwiftUI ŌĆō Liquid Glass Bottom Menu Bar

```swift
import SwiftUI

struct LiquidGlassMenuBar: View {
    var body: some View {
        ZStack {
            // Your main content
            ScrollView {
                VStack(spacing: 24) {
                    ForEach(0..<40) { i in
                        RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 16)
                            .fill(Color.blue.opacity(0.2))
                            .frame(height: 80)
                            .overlay(Text("Row \(i)"))
                            .padding(.horizontal)
                    }
                    .padding(.top, 16)
                }
            }

            // Glass menu bar
            VStack {
                Spacer()
                HStack(spacing: 40) {
                    Image(systemName: "house.fill")
                    Image(systemName: "magnifyingglass")
                    Image(systemName: "heart.fill")
                    Image(systemName: "person.fill")
                }
                .font(.system(size: 18, weight: .semibold))
                .foregroundStyle(.white)
                .frame(height: 60)
                .frame(maxWidth: 320)
                .background(
                    // Glass / liquid material
                    .ultraThinMaterial
                )
                .clipShape(RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 26, style: .continuous))
                .overlay(
                    RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 26, style: .continuous)
                        .stroke(.white.opacity(0.25), lineWidth: 1)
                )
                .shadow(radius: 18, y: 10)
                .padding(.bottom, 20)
            }
            .ignoresSafeArea(.keyboard, edges: .bottom) // stays above keyboard
        }
    }
}

struct LiquidGlassMenuBar_Previews: PreviewProvider {
    static var previews: some View {
        LiquidGlassMenuBar()
    }
}
```

**Key parts:**

- `.background(.ultraThinMaterial)` ŌåÆ the iOS ŌĆ£glassŌĆØ blur.
- `clipShape(RoundedRectangle(...))` ŌåÆ soft ŌĆ£liquidŌĆØ capsule look.
- `.overlay(...stroke...)` ŌåÆ subtle white border like polished glass.
- `.shadow(radius:y:)` ŌåÆ makes it float above content.

You can tweak:

- **Opacity**: add `.opacity(0.9)` on the background for more/less glass.
- **Tint**: layer a color under the material:

```swift
.background(
    ZStack {
        Color.blue.opacity(0.25)
        .ultraThinMaterial
    }
)
```

---

## UIKit ŌĆō Liquid Glass Bar (e.g. custom tab/menu bar)

For UIKit (iOS 13+), use `UIVisualEffectView` with `UIBlurEffect` and optional vibrancy.

```swift
final class LiquidGlassMenuBarView: UIView {
    private let blurView = UIVisualEffectView(effect: UIBlurEffect(style: .systemUltraThinMaterial))
    private let stack = UIStackView()

    override init(frame: CGRect) {
        super.init(frame: frame)
        setup()
    }

    required init?(coder: NSCoder) {
        super.init(coder: coder)
        setup()
    }

    private func setup() {
        // Rounded + ŌĆ£liquidŌĆØ shape
        layer.cornerRadius = 26
        layer.masksToBounds = true

        // Glass blur
        blurView.frame = bounds
        blurView.autoresizingMask = [.flexibleWidth, .flexibleHeight]
        addSubview(blurView)

        // Subtle border
        layer.borderColor = UIColor.white.withAlphaComponent(0.25).cgColor
        layer.borderWidth = 1

        // Shadow outside the view (so not masked)
        // Have the container view (outside) apply the shadow.
    }
}
```

Then in your view controller:

```swift
class ViewController: UIViewController {

    private let glassBar = LiquidGlassMenuBarView()

    override func viewDidLoad() {
        super.viewDidLoad()

        view.addSubview(glassBar)
        glassBar.translatesAutoresizingMaskIntoConstraints = false

        NSLayoutConstraint.activate([
            glassBar.heightAnchor.constraint(equalToConstant: 60),
            glassBar.leadingAnchor.constraint(equalTo: view.leadingAnchor, constant: 24),
            glassBar.trailingAnchor.constraint(equalTo: view.trailingAnchor, constant: -24),
            glassBar.bottomAnchor.constraint(equalTo: view.safeAreaLayoutGuide.bottomAnchor, constant: -12)
        ])

        // Shadow on wrapper container if you want a ŌĆ£floatingŌĆØ effect
        glassBar.superview?.layer.shadowColor = UIColor.black.cgColor
        glassBar.superview?.layer.shadowOpacity = 0.25
        glassBar.superview?.layer.shadowRadius = 16
        glassBar.superview?.layer.shadowOffset = CGSize(width: 0, height: 10)
    }
}
```

Inside `LiquidGlassMenuBarView` youŌĆÖd add your buttons (UIStackView with icons) on top of `blurView.contentView`.

---

If you tell me whether youŌĆÖre building in **SwiftUI or UIKit**, I can give you a drop-in `MenuBar` component tailored to your project (with selection state, animations, etc.).

## User

I mean the iOS 26 Liquid Glass

---

## Assistant

Gotcha, Mr. White ŌĆö youŌĆÖre talking about the **new Liquid Glass design in iOS 26**, not the old `.ultraThinMaterial` stuff.

HereŌĆÖs the short version:  
On **iOS 26+, you should use the new `glassEffect` APIs + `GlassEffectContainer`** to build a floating, Liquid Glass style menu/tab bar. System tab bars get this for free, but for a custom one you wire it up yourself.

---

## 1. Easiest way: use `TabView` and let iOS 26 do it

If you just need a standard bottom tab bar, you often **donŌĆÖt have to do anything**: build a normal `TabView` and run on iOS 26 ŌĆö the system tab bar automatically adopts Liquid Glass. ŅłĆciteŅłéturn2search4Ņłéturn2search5Ņłü

```swift
@available(iOS 26.0, *)
struct LiquidGlassTabAppView: View {
    var body: some View {
        TabView {
            Text("Home")
                .tabItem {
                    Label("Home", systemImage: "house.fill")
                }

            Text("Search")
                .tabItem {
                    Label("Search", systemImage: "magnifyingglass")
                }

            Text("Profile")
                .tabItem {
                    Label("Me", systemImage: "person.fill")
                }
        }
        // iOS 26 will render the tab bar in Liquid Glass automatically
    }
}
```

If all you want is ŌĆ£menu bar at bottom with Liquid Glass lookŌĆØ, this is the most ŌĆ£Apple-blessedŌĆØ route.

---

## 2. Custom **Liquid Glass menu bar** (SwiftUI, iOS 26+)

If you want a **floating pill-shaped menu bar** (like the new toolbars in AppleŌĆÖs examples), use `GlassEffectContainer` + `.glassEffect(...)`. ŅłĆciteŅłéturn7search7Ņłéturn7search9Ņłéturn2search4Ņłü

```swift
import SwiftUI

@available(iOS 26.0, *)
struct LiquidGlassMenuBarExample: View {
    @State private var selected = 0

    var body: some View {
        ZStack {
            // Your main scrolling content
            ScrollView {
                VStack(spacing: 24) {
                    ForEach(0..<30) { i in
                        RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 16)
                            .fill(Color.blue.opacity(0.15))
                            .frame(height: 80)
                            .overlay(Text("Row \(i)"))
                            .padding(.horizontal)
                    }
                    .padding(.top, 40)
                }
            }

            // Floating Liquid Glass menu bar
            VStack {
                Spacer()

                GlassEffectContainer {
                    HStack(spacing: 32) {
                        tabItem("house.fill", tag: 0)
                        tabItem("magnifyingglass", tag: 1)
                        tabItem("heart.fill", tag: 2)
                        tabItem("person.fill", tag: 3)
                    }
                    .padding(.horizontal, 20)
                    .padding(.vertical, 10)
                    .glassEffect(
                        .regular
                            .interactive(true)                // reacts to touches
                            .tint(.blue.opacity(0.35)),       // subtle color tint
                        in: RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 26, style: .continuous)
                    )
                }
                .padding(.bottom, 16)
            }
            .ignoresSafeArea(.keyboard, edges: .bottom)
        }
    }

    @ViewBuilder
    private func tabItem(_ systemName: String, tag: Int) -> some View {
        let isSelected = (selected == tag)

        Button {
            selected = tag
        } label: {
            Image(systemName: systemName)
                .font(.system(size: 18, weight: .semibold))
                .symbolRenderingMode(.hierarchical)
                .foregroundStyle(isSelected ? Color.accentColor : .secondary)
                .frame(width: 32, height: 32)
        }
        .buttonStyle(.glass)   // Liquid Glass button style in iOS 26
    }
}
```

**Why this matches iOS 26 Liquid Glass:**

- `.glassEffect(...)` is the official Liquid Glass modifier for custom views. ŅłĆciteŅłéturn7search7Ņłéturn7search5Ņłü  
- `GlassEffectContainer` groups multiple glass shapes so they render as **one continuous, morphable glass surface**, just like the new tab/tool bars. ŅłĆciteŅłéturn7search9Ņłéturn7search3Ņłü  
- `.regular.interactive(true).tint(...)` gives you:
  - the standard Liquid Glass look
  - touch ŌĆ£squishŌĆØ interactions
  - a subtle color tint instead of plain white glass. ŅłĆciteŅłéturn7search7Ņłéturn7search4Ņłü  

---

## 3. Supporting iOS 25 and earlier (fallback)

If you need to support older OS versions, wrap the Liquid Glass bits in `#available` and fall back to `Material`:

```swift
struct MenuBarWrapper: View {
    var body: some View {
        if #available(iOS 26.0, *) {
            LiquidGlassMenuBarExample()
        } else {
            // Older look: normal blurred pill
            ZStack {
                // content ŌĆ”

                VStack {
                    Spacer()
                    HStack(spacing: 32) {
                        Image(systemName: "house.fill")
                        Image(systemName: "magnifyingglass")
                        Image(systemName: "heart.fill")
                        Image(systemName: "person.fill")
                    }
                    .font(.system(size: 18, weight: .semibold))
                    .foregroundStyle(.white)
                    .padding(.horizontal, 20)
                    .padding(.vertical, 10)
                    .background(.ultraThinMaterial,
                                in: RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 26, style: .continuous))
                    .padding(.bottom, 16)
                }
            }
        }
    }
}
```

---

If you tell me **exactly what layout** you want (full-width like system tab bar vs floating pill vs side dock), I can rewrite this into a drop-in `LiquidGlassMenuBar` component you can just drop into your project.
